When Kharaj Is Not Due and When It Is Due Due to Neglect
Ruling on exemption from kharaj due to calamities and obligation upon neglect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which kharaj (land tax) is waived or remains due, and apply the Hanafi principle distinguishing actual growth (ushr) from potential growth (kharaj).

Core Idea
Kharaj is based on potential growth, not actual harvest; only unpreventable calamities waive it.

Land taxation in Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between kharaj (tax on conquered land) and ushr (tithe on voluntary converts' land). While ushr is due only on actual produce, kharaj is due on the land's ability to produce. This lesson examines when calamities or owner neglect affect the liability for kharaj and lays out the critical principle that only unpreventable disasters exempt the landowner.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of land tax
Kharaj is levied on conquered lands; it may be fixed (muwazzaf) or proportional (muqasamah). Ushr is a tithe on lands of voluntary converts. Both have different bases of obligation.
Kharaj al-muqasamah and ushr look similar but differ in legal basis.
2
Determine when exemption applies
Exemption occurs if water is cut off, land is overwhelmed, or a calamity (afah) strikes. A calamity must be 'heavenly' (fire, flood, extreme cold) or non-heavenly but unpreventable (locusts).
Preventable damage (e.g., from beasts, mice) does not cancel kharaj.
3
Distinguish actual vs potential growth
Ushr is based on actual growth (nima' tahqiqi): no produce, no tithe. Kharaj is based on potential growth (nima' taqdiri): the land's capacity to yield, not actual yield.
This principle explains why owner neglect still incurs kharaj.
4
Apply to cases of owner neglect or inability
If the owner abandons cultivable land, kharaj remains due. If land is naturally unsuitable (saline, no water) and cannot be improved, kharaj falls. If the owner is unable, the imam may intervene.
The imam's options include sharecropping, leasing, or even selling to recover kharaj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا خراج لو انقطع الماء عن أرضه، أو غلب عليها، أو أصاب الزرع آفة، ويجب إن عطلها مالكها

[١] قوله : ولا خراج؛ أي لا يجب خراج لا خراج موظف ولا خراج مقاسمة، ولا العشر، وعدم العشر خراجُ المقاسمة ظاهر لتعلّق الواجب فيهما بعين الخارج، في «الفتاوي الخيرية».

[٢] قوله : آفة؛ أي سماوية كحرق وغرق وشدّة برد، فإن كانت غير سماوية، فإن كانت مما لا يمكن الاحتراز عنها كأكل الجراد، فكذلك وإن كان الاحتراز عنها ممكناً كأكل سباع وقردة وفأرة ونحو ذلك لا يسقط الخراج، كما لا يسقط إذا هلك الخارج بعد الحصاد، كذا في «منح الغفار»، و«البحر».

[٣] قوله : ويجب...الخ؛ الأصلُ في هذا الباب أنّ المعتبر في وجوب العشر هو النماء التحقيقي، وفي الخراج النماء التقديري فإذا عدّل المالك الأرض الصالحة للزراعة ولم يزرع لا يجب العشر، ويجب الخراج؛ لوجود قدرته ووجوبه في الذمة بالتمكن من الزراعة.

وفي «الخانية»: له في أرض الخراج سبخة لا تصلح للزراعة، أو لا يصلحها الماء، إن أمكنه إصلاحها ولم يصلح فعليه الخراج وإلا فلا، ولو عجز المالك عن الزراعة لعدم قوّته وأسبابه فللإمام أن يدفعها لغيره مزارعة؛ ليأخذ الخراج من نصيب المالك ويمسك الباقي للمالك، وإن شاء أجرها وأخذ الخراج من الأجرة، وإن شاء زرعها من بيت المال، فإن لم يتمكن باعها وأخذ الخراج من ثمنها، كذا في «النهاية».
And there is no kharaj if the water is cut off from his land, or it is overwhelmed, or the crop is afflicted by a calamity, and it is obligatory if its owner neglects it. [1] He said: 'and there is no kharaj' means there is no kharaj—neither fixed kharaj nor proportional kharaj—nor the tithe, and the absence of tithe in proportional kharaj is apparent because the obligation in both is attached to the actual produce, as in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyya. [2] He said: 'a calamity' means a heavenly one like fire, drowning, and severe cold; if it is non-heavenly, if it cannot be guarded against like locusts, it is likewise; but if it can be guarded against like predation by beasts, monkeys, mice, and the like, it does not cancel the kharaj, just as it is not cancelled if the produce is destroyed after harvest, as in Minah al-Ghaffar and al-Bahr. [3] He said: 'and it is obligatory...' etc.; the principle in this chapter is that regarding the obligation of tithe, actual growth is considered, and regarding kharaj, potential growth is considered. So if the owner abandons land suitable for cultivation and does not sow, tithe is not obligatory, but kharaj is obligatory because of his ability and its obligation being in his liability due to being able to cultivate. And in al-Khaniyya: if he has saline land in kharaj land that is not suitable for cultivation, or water does not make it suitable, if he can improve it and does not, he is liable for kharaj; otherwise not. And if the owner is unable to cultivate due to lack of strength and means, the imam may give it to another for sharecropping, take the kharaj from the owner's share and keep the remainder for the owner; or he may lease it and take the kharaj from the rent; or he may cultivate it from the treasury; if he cannot, he may sell it and take the kharaj from its price, as in al-Nihaya.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on when kharaj (land tax) is not due and when it becomes due due to the owner's neglect. The commentary explains that the exemption applies to both types of kharaj: 'kharaj muwazzaf' (fixed tax) and 'kharaj muqasamah' (proportional tax), as well as 'ushr' (tithe). The term 'afah' (calamity) refers to heavenly disasters like fire, flood, or extreme cold. If the calamity is non-heavenly but unpreventable, like locusts, the exemption still applies. However, if it is preventable, like damage from predators, monkeys, or mice, the kharaj is not cancelled, just as it is not cancelled if the crop is lost after harvest. The underlying principle is that for ushr, actual growth (nima' tahqiqi) is considered, while for kharaj, potential growth (nima' taqdiri) is considered. Therefore, if the owner neglects to cultivate fertile land, ushr is not due but kharaj remains due because of his ability and the obligation being in his liability. The commentary also discusses cases of saline land or lack of water, and the imam's options if the owner is unable to cultivate.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on conquered lands; it is a fixed or proportional levy on the land itself.
عشر (‘ushr): Tithe, a tax of one-tenth on agricultural produce from lands whose owners accepted Islam voluntarily.
آفة (āfah): Calamity afflicting the crop; divided into heavenly (fire, flood, cold) and non-heavenly (locusts, predators, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following does NOT cancel kharaj?
A) Flood destroying the crop
B) Locust swarm eating the crop
C) Owner failing to irrigate and crop fails
D) Extreme cold killing the plants

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is due on land capable of cultivation; only unpreventable calamities exempt, not owner neglect or preventable losses.

Kharaj Remains Despite Islam and Distinction from Ushr
Ruling that kharaj continues on land when the owner converts to Islam or a Muslim buys it, and no ushr is due on its produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why kharaj continues on conquered land even if the owner becomes Muslim, and differentiate kharaj from ushr in terms of cause and locus.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a right on the land, not a personal tax; it continues regardless of religion.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah addresses a critical rule in the Hanafi school: land tax (kharaj) on conquered lands is not tied to the owner's religion. Even if the non-Muslim owner converts to Islam, or a Muslim purchases the land, kharaj remains obligatory. Moreover, the produce of such land is not subject to tithe ('ushr), because kharaj and ushr are mutually exclusive on the same land. The passage then explains the rationale and contrasts the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling that kharaj remains on the land and no ushr is due on its produce when the owner becomes Muslim or a Muslim buys the land.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i holds the opposite view: kharaj is waived upon Islam.
Shafi'is view kharaj as a personal tax on non-Muslims.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the evidence: practice of the Sahaba (Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, al-Husayn) who bought kharaj lands and paid kharaj, and the principle 'al-ibqa' ashal min al-ibtida' (maintaining is easier than initiating).
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted proof).
4
Analyze the distinction between kharaj and ushr
Understand that kharaj and ushr differ in essence (worship vs. punishment), cause (actual vs. potential growth), and locus (produce vs. dhimma). They cannot coexist on the same land because the land cannot be both conquered (anwatan) and surrendered (sulhan).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: a Muslim owning kharaj land pays kharaj under Hanafi, but would pay ushr under Shafi'i.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبقى إن أسلم المالك، أو شراها مسلم، ولا عشر في خارج أرضه: أي أرض الخراج، وهذا عندنا، وعند الشافعي خلافه.

[١] قوله : ويبقى؛ يعني إن أسلم الكافر الذي عليه خراج في أرضه أو اشترى الأرض الخراجية منه مسلم يجب عليها الخراج كما كان، وقد ثبت في كتاب «المعرفة» للبيهقي، وكتاب «الخراج» وغيرهما: «أنّ جمعاً من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم كابن مسعود وخباب والحسين اشتروا أراضي الخراج فكانوا يؤدون خراجها». والسر فيه: أن الإبقاء أسهل من الابتداء، فلا بأس ببقاء الخراج على المسلم، وإن لم يكن وظيفة المسلم ابتداء.

[٢] قوله : يجب؛ لأن العشر والخراج حقان مختلفان من حيث الذات؛ فإنّ الأول مؤنة فيها معنى العبادة، والثاني مؤنة فيها معنى العقوبة، ووجوبهما بسببين مختلفين، فإن سبب العشر الأرض النامية بالحقيقة، وسبب الخراج النامية بالتمكن، ومحلّهما أيضاً مختلف، فإنّ العشر محله الخارج، والخراج محلّه ذمة المالك، حتى لو لم يخرج شيء بتعطيله وجب الخراج، وإذا كان هذا هكذا، فلا يمنع وجوب أحدهما وجوب الآخر. ونحن نقول: سبب الحقين واحد وهو الأرض النامية، غاية الأمر أنه اعتبر في العشر تحقق النّماء، وفي الخراج تقديره، وبينهما تناف من وجه، فإنّ الخراج يجب في أرض فتحت عنوةً وقهراً، والعشر في أرض أسلم أهلها طوعاً، والوصفان لا يجتمعان في أرض واحدة.
And it remains if the owner becomes Muslim, or a Muslim buys it, and there is no ushr on the produce of his land: meaning land of kharaj. This is our position, and according to al-Shafi'i, it is otherwise. [1] He said: 'and it remains' means if the non-Muslim who owes kharaj on his land becomes Muslim or a Muslim buys the kharaj land from him, kharaj is obligatory on the land as before, and it is confirmed in the book al-Ma'rifah by al-Bayhaqi and Kitab al-Kharaj and others that 'a group of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, such as Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, and al-Husayn, bought kharaj lands and they used to pay its kharaj.' The secret in it is that maintaining is easier than instituting, so there is no harm in the continuation of kharaj on a Muslim, even if it was not a function of a Muslim initially. [2] He said: 'it is obligatory' because ushr and kharaj are two different rights in essence; the first is a levy with a meaning of worship, the second a levy with a meaning of punishment, and their obligation arises from different causes: the cause of ushr is land that actually grows, and the cause of kharaj is land that has potential growth. Their loci are also different: ushr's locus is the produce, kharaj's locus is the owner's liability, so that if nothing comes out due to his neglect, kharaj is obligatory. And since this is the case, the obligation of one does not prevent the obligation of the other. And we say: the cause of both rights is one, which is productive land; the only difference is that in ushr, actual growth is considered, and in kharaj, potential growth; and there is a mutual exclusivity between them in one respect, for kharaj is obligated on land conquered by force and compulsion, and ushr on land whose people submitted voluntarily, and the two descriptions do not come together in a single land.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage establishes that kharaj (land tax) continues to be levied on land even if the landowner converts to Islam or if a Muslim purchases kharaj land. The produce of such land is not subject to ushr (tithe). This is the Hanafi position, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kharaj is waived upon the owner's Islam or purchase by a Muslim. The Hanafi evidence includes the practice of several Sahaba (Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, and others) who bought kharaj lands and continued to pay kharaj. The underlying rationale (sirr) is that it is easier to maintain an existing obligation than to initiate a new one. The commentary then explains that ushr and kharaj are distinct in essence: ushr has a connotation of worship (ibadah), while kharaj has a connotation of punishment (uqubah). They arise from different causes: ushr from actual growth, kharaj from potential growth. Their loci differ: ushr attaches to the produce (kharij), kharaj attaches to the landowner's liability (dhimma). Therefore, the presence of one does not negate the other. However, the Hanafi position is that the underlying cause for both is the land's productivity, but they differ in the type of growth considered (actual vs. potential) and the historical origin (kharaj on conquered lands, ushr on lands surrendered peacefully). Thus, they cannot coexist on the same land.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax on conquered lands; it continues even if the owner becomes Muslim or sells to a Muslim.
عشر (‘ushr): Tithe on agricultural produce; it is not due on land subject to kharaj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a Muslim purchases kharaj land?
A) Kharaj is waived.
B) Kharaj remains and no ushr is due.
C) Both kharaj and ushr become due.
D) Only ushr is due.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a perpetual land right that continues even if the owner becomes Muslim, and it excludes ushr on the same land.

Kharaj Remains on Muslim-Owned Land: The Hanafi View
Explaining the Hanafi ruling and dispute with Shafi'is

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that kharaj remains on Muslim-owned conquered land and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Kharaj and 'ushr differ in nature, cause, and locus; thus kharaj remains on conquered land even if owned by a Muslim.

When a non-Muslim owner of kharaj land embraces Islam, or a Muslim purchases such land, does the kharaj fall? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling that kharaj remains, supported by Companion practice and a deep legal analysis distinguishing kharaj from 'ushr. You will also encounter the Shafi'i position and understand the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: kharaj remains on land conquered by force (anwatan) even when the owner becomes Muslim or a Muslim buys it; no 'ushr is due on the produce.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that kharaj falls upon Islam or Muslim ownership, and 'ushr becomes due instead. If the land remains uncultivated, the state may cultivate it from the treasury.
The text has a lacuna at 'عند الشافعي:', but the meaning is reconstructed from context.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof: Companion practice
The author cites that Companions like Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, and al-Husayn bought kharaj lands and continued paying kharaj after becoming Muslims. This is recorded in al-Bayhaqi's 'al-Ma'rifah' and other sources.
This is a qawl sahabi, considered strong but not qat'i thubut.
4
Analyse the Hanafi legal reasoning (talil)
The author distinguishes 'ushr and kharaj by three criteria: nature (ibadah vs uqubah), cause (actual vs potential productivity), and locus (produce vs owner's liability). Because they differ in these aspects, they do not preclude each other.
The author also notes that the basis of land classification (anwatan vs sulhan) differs: kharaj land is conquered by force, 'ushr land by voluntary submission; they cannot combine.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically: under Hanafi, a Muslim landowner pays kharaj (fixed or share-cropping) and no 'ushr. Under Shafi'i, he pays 'ushr and no kharaj; if land lies fallow, the state may cultivate it.
The author also distinguishes fixed kharaj (muwazzaf, annual) from share-cropping kharaj (muqasamah, repeats like 'ushr), clarifying that the dispute concerns both types.

ويتكرر العشر بتكرر الخارج، بخلاف الخراج، فإنّه لا يتكرر، واعلم أن الخراج نوعان : خراج موظف، وهو الوظيفة المعينة التي توضع على الأرض كما وضع عمر رضي الله عنه على سواد العراق، وخراج المقاسمة، كربع الخارج، وخمسه، ونحوهما، فالذي لا يتكرر هو الموظف، أما خراج المقاسمة فهو يتكرر كالعشر. ويشهد لمذهبنا ما أخرجه ابن عدي في «الكامل»، مرفوعاً: «لا يجتمع على مسلم خراج وعشر»، لكن سنده ضعيف جداً، كما بسطه الزيلعي وغيره. قوله : ويتكرر؛ يعني لو تكرّر الخارج من الأرض في سنة واحدة تكرّر العشر؛ لوجوبه في كلّ خارج، بخلاف الخراج، فإنّه في ذمة المالك في كل سنة، فلا يتكرّر بتكرّر الخارج، فالخراج له شدّة من حيث المقاسمة؛ والفرق بينه وبين الموظف بوجوه: منها: إنّ الثاني كالعشر مأخذاً لتعلقه بالخارج، فيؤخذ من كل ما يؤخذ منه العشر أو نصفه من الرطاب والزروع والكروم والنخيل وغير ذلك، بخلاف الأول؛ فإنّه على الأرض لا تعلّق له بما يخرج. ومنها: إنّ الثاني يتكرر بتكرّر الخارج في السنة بخلاف الأول.
And it remains if the owner becomes Muslim, or a Muslim buys it, and there is no 'ushr on its produce: meaning kharaj land. This is our view, and according to al-Shafi'i: [?] cultivated from the treasury, and if not possible, he sells it and takes the kharaj from its price, as in 'al-Nihayah'. He said: 'it remains' means if a non-Muslim who has kharaj on his land becomes Muslim, or a Muslim buys the kharaj land from him, kharaj is obligatory on it as before, and it is established in the book 'al-Ma'rifah' of al-Bayhaqi and 'Kitab al-Kharaj' and others: 'A group of the Companions, such as Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, and al-Husayn, bought kharaj lands and paid their kharaj.' The secret is that preservation is easier than initiation, so there is no harm in kharaj remaining on a Muslim, even though it is not the initial duty of a Muslim. He said: 'it is obligatory' because 'ushr and kharaj are different rights in essence; the first is a levy with the meaning of worship, and the second is a levy with the meaning of punishment, and their obligation is due to different causes, for the cause of 'ushr is land that is actually productive, and the cause of kharaj is land that is potentially productive, and their loci are also different, for the locus of 'ushr is the produce, and the locus of kharaj is the liability of the owner, such that if nothing is produced due to neglect, kharaj is still obligatory. Since this is the case, the obligation of one does not prevent the obligation of the other. And we say: The cause of both rights is one, namely productive land, except that in 'ushr actual growth is considered, and in kharaj potential growth is considered, and there is a contradiction in one respect, for kharaj is obligatory on land conquered by force and compulsion, and 'ushr on land whose inhabitants became Muslim willingly, and the two descriptions are not combined in one piece of land. And 'ushr is repeated by the repetition of the produce, unlike kharaj, for it is not repeated. Know that kharaj is of two types: fixed kharaj (muwazzaf), which is the specific duty placed on the land as 'Umar placed on the Sawad of Iraq, and share-cropping kharaj (muqasamah), like a quarter or a fifth of the produce and the like. What is not repeated is the fixed type; as for the share-cropping kharaj, it is repeated like 'ushr. Supporting our madhhab is what Ibn 'Adi narrated in 'al-Kamil' as marfu': 'Kharaj and 'ushr are not combined on a Muslim,' but its chain is very weak, as al-Zayla'i and others explained. He said: 'and it is repeated' means if the produce of the land is repeated in one year, 'ushr is repeated, because it is obligatory on every produce, unlike kharaj, for it is on the liability of the owner each year, so it is not repeated by the repetition of produce. Thus kharaj has severity in that it is attached to potential, and lightness in that it is not repeated in the year, even if he cultivates it many times; and 'ushr has severity in its repetition by repetition of produce, and lightness in its attachment to the very produce, so if he neglects it, nothing is taken from him. This is in 'al-Fath'. He said: 'and share-cropping kharaj'; the difference between it and the fixed type is in several aspects: from them, the second is like 'ushr in origin because it is attached to the produce, so it is taken from everything from which 'ushr or half of it is taken, such as vegetables, grains, vines, palm trees, and other things, unlike the first, for it is on the land and has no attachment to what is produced. And from them, the second is repeated by the repetition of produce in the year, unlike the first.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah, addressing the ruling on kharaj land when the owner becomes Muslim or a Muslim purchases it. The author begins by stating the Hanafi position: kharaj remains on the land, and no 'ushr is due on its produce. He then contrasts this with the Shafi'i view (which is unclear in the text due to corruption but likely holds that 'ushr replaces kharaj, and if the land remains uncultivated, the state cultivates it). The proof for the Hanafi position is the practice of the Companions (Ibn Mas'ud, Khabbab, al-Husayn) who bought kharaj lands and continued paying kharaj, as recorded in al-Bayhaqi's 'al-Ma'rifah' and other works. The author then explains the wisdom: retaining kharaj is easier than initiating a new tax. Next, he gives the legal reasoning: 'ushr and kharaj are fundamentally different. 'Ushr is a levy with the meaning of worship (ibadah), attached to actual produce (kharj), and its cause is land that is actually productive (al-namiyah bi'l-haqiqah). Kharaj is a levy with the meaning of punishment (uqubah), attached to the liability of the owner (dhimma), and its cause is land that is potentially productive (al-namiyah bi'l-tamakkun). Therefore, they do not prevent each other. The author then addresses a potential objection: the Shafi'is might argue that the causes are one (the same land), but the Hanafis respond that the basis of fatah (conquest) differs: kharaj land is conquered by force ('anwatan), while 'ushr land is where the inhabitants submitted voluntarily. They cannot combine. The discussion then moves to the repetition of 'ushr versus kharaj. 'Ushr repeats with each harvest, while fixed kharaj (muwazzaf) is a fixed annual sum regardless of the number of harvests. The author distinguishes two types of kharaj: fixed (muwazzaf) and share-cropping (muqasamah). Share-cropping kharaj, being a percentage of produce, does repeat like 'ushr. The author also mentions a weak hadith supporting the Hanafi position but notes its weakness. Finally, he elaborates on the differences between fixed and share-cropping kharaj: the latter is like 'ushr in being attached to produce, taken from a variety of crops, and repeating with each harvest.

Key Terms
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax imposed on conquered (anwatan) lands, paid by the landholder regardless of religion, and based on the land's productive capacity.
العشر (al-'ushr): A tithe (10% or 5%) on the produce of land whose inhabitants accepted Islam voluntarily (sulhan), considered an act of worship.
خراج موظف (kharaj muwazzaf): Fixed annual land tax assessed on the land itself, not on the produce, as set by Caliph 'Umar on the Sawad of Iraq.
خراج مقاسمة (kharaj muqasamah): Share-cropping kharaj, a percentage (e.g., quarter, fifth) of the produce, which is taken like 'ushr and repeats with each harvest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to kharaj when a Muslim purchases kharaj land?
A) Kharaj falls and 'ushr becomes due on the produce.
B) Kharaj remains and no 'ushr is due on the produce.
C) Both kharaj and 'ushr are due on the produce.
D) The land becomes tax-free.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj remains on conquered land even if owned by a Muslim, because its cause (potential productivity), locus (owner's liability), and nature (uqubah) differ fundamentally from 'ushr.

Types of Jizya and Its Quranic Basis
Introduction to jizya: its two types and Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of jizya in Hanafi fiqh and cite the Quranic proof for its obligation.

Core Idea
Jizya is of two types: treaty-fixed (immutable) and Imam-imposed; its basis is the Quranic command to fight until payment.

In this passage, we examine the classification of jizya (head tax on non-Muslim subjects) into two distinct types. The Hanafi school distinguishes between jizya set by mutual peace treaty and jizya imposed by the Imam after conquest. We will also explore the primary evidence from Surah al-Tawbah that establishes the legitimacy of jizya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of jizya
From the matn (base text): jizya is either set by mutual agreement (sulh) or imposed by the Imam after conquest. Note that the treaty-fixed jizya is immutable.
The commentary expands on the first type with the example of the Prophet's treaty with Najran.
2
Understand the ruling for each type
The first type is fixed and cannot be changed; the second is determined by the Imam according to ijtihad. Both are wajib on eligible dhimmis.
The term 'jizya' itself indicates it suffices in place of killing.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The primary evidence is Surah al-Tawbah 9:29, which commands fighting the People of the Book until they pay jizya. The imperative indicates obligation, and the condition 'until they give jizya' establishes the tax as the alternative to warfare.
The verse is qati' al-thubut (definite transmission) but zanni al-dalalah (interpretable) as to the exact details.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الجزية
ما وُضِعَتْ بصلح لا تغير، وحين غُلِبُوا وأُقِرُّوا على أملاكهم توضع على كتابي

اعلم أن الجزية نوعان: جزية وضعت بالتراضي، فتقدر بحسب ما يقع عليه الاتفاق. وجزية يبتدأ الإمام وضعها إذا غلب عليهم.

قوله: فصل الجزية؛ لما فرغ من ذكر الوظائف المتعلقة بالأراضي شرع في ذكر الوظيفة التي توظف على رؤوس الكفار، ويقال لها: خراج الرأس، والجزية – بالكسر – لأنها تكفي وتجزئ عن القتل، وجمعه جِزًى كَلِحْيَةٍ وَلِحًى، كذا في «البحر».
قوله: الاتفاق؛ أي بين المسلمين وبين الكفار كما صالح رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نصارى نجران على ألفي حلة النصف في صفر، والبقية في رجب يؤدونها إلى المسلمين، وعارية ثلاثين درعاً.
قوله: وأقروا؛ أي أقرهم الإمام على أراضيهم وأملاكهم.
قوله: توضع؛ الأصل في هذا الباب قوله تعالى: {قَاتِلُوا الَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَلَا بِالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَلَا يُحَرِّمُونَ مَا حَرَّمَ اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ وَلَا يَدِينُونَ دِينَ الْحَقِّ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ عَن يَدٍ وَهُمْ صَاغِرُونَ} [التوبة: 29]، قال مجاهد: نزلت هذه حين أمر محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه لله بغزوة تبوك، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن جرير وغيرهما.
Chapter of Jizya. Whatever is set by treaty is not changed. And when they are overpowered and are confirmed upon their properties, it is imposed upon the People of the Book. Know that jizya is of two types: (1) Jizya set by mutual consent, so it is determined according to what agreement is reached upon. (2) Jizya that the Imam initiates its imposition when he overpowers them. [Commentary:] His statement: 'Chapter of Jizya' — when he finished mentioning the obligations related to lands, he began to mention the obligation that is imposed upon the heads of the disbelievers, and it is called 'land tax on the head', and 'al-jizyah' (with kasrah) because it suffices and suffices in place of killing, and its plural is 'jizan' like 'lihyah' and 'lihan', as in 'al-Bahr'. His statement: 'agreement' — meaning between Muslims and disbelievers, as the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, made peace with the Christians of Najran for two thousand garments, half in Safar and the remainder in Rajab, which they pay to the Muslims, and a loan of thirty coats of mail. His statement: 'and they are confirmed' — meaning the Imam confirms them upon their lands and properties. His statement: 'it is imposed' — the basis of this chapter is His statement: 'Fight those who do not believe in Allah and in the Last Day and do not make unlawful what Allah and His Messenger have made unlawful and do not adopt the religion of truth from those who were given the Scripture until they give the jizyah willingly while they are humbled' — Mujahid said: This was revealed when Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and his Companions were commanded to go to the expedition of Tabuk, narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ibn Jarir, and others.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the chapter of jizya. It first states the two types of jizya: (1) that which is set by a peace treaty (sulh) and cannot be changed afterward, and (2) that which the Imam imposes on the conquered people after their defeat and subjugation. The term 'jizya' is explained as a head tax on non-Muslims, derived from the root meaning 'to suffice' because it suffices in place of killing. The commentator then explains the proof from the Qur'an, citing verse 9:29 which commands fighting the People of the Book until they pay jizya. This verse is the primary evidence for the legitimacy and obligation of collecting jizya. The commentary also references the historical precedent of the Prophet's treaty with the Christians of Najran.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A head tax imposed on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in an Islamic state, which suffices in place of killing.
صلح (sulh): A peace treaty between Muslims and non-Muslims that may include terms for jizya.
كتابي (kitabi): A person who has a revealed scripture (Jew, Christian, etc.) upon whom jizya is imposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to jizya that is fixed by a peace treaty?
A) It can be changed by the Imam if needed.
B) It is fixed and cannot be changed.
C) It is only valid if the non-Muslims agree to increase it.
D) It is abolished after one year.

Key Takeaway
Jizya is of two types: treaty-fixed (immutable) and Imam-imposed; its obligation is proven by the Quranic command in Surah al-Tawbah.

The Two Types of Jizya and Its Recipients
Defines jizya types and provides proofs for Kitabis and Majus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of jizya, identify who must pay it (Kitabis and Majus), and cite the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
Jizya is a head tax on non-Muslims: either fixed by treaty or set by the imam; taken from Kitabis by Quran and from Majus by Sunnah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the two categories of jizya: one settled by mutual agreement and one imposed by the imam after conquest. It then establishes that jizya is taken from People of the Book (Kitabis) based on the Quranic command, and from Magians (Majus) based on the Prophet's practice. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of jizya and avoiding common misconceptions about the status of Majus.

Guided Path
1
Define jizya and its linguistic root
The author notes that jizya comes from a root meaning 'to suffice' because it substitutes for killing. Identify this as the head tax on non-Muslims.
Also called kharaj al-ra's.
2
Distinguish the two types of jizya
Type 1: jizya set by treaty (sulh) – amount is fixed by mutual agreement and cannot be changed. Type 2: jizya imposed by the imam after conquest (anwatan) – amount is determined by ijtihad.
Treaty-based jizya is permanent; the imam cannot alter it.
3
Identify the primary recipients: Kitabis
The matn limits jizya to Kitabis. The commentary provides the Quranic proof (al-Tawbah 9:29) and explains that it includes Jews, Christians, Samaritans, and Franks.
The verse commands fighting until they pay jizya.
4
Extend to Majus via Sunnah
Although not Kitabis, Majus (Zoroastrians) are included based on the Prophet's practice of taking jizya from the Magians of Hajar, as reported in Sahih al-Bukhari.
‘Umar initially hesitated until he heard the hadith.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not take jizya from Majus because they are not People of the Book. The Hanafi school relies on the prophetic practice as a separate proof.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for dhimmi status.

فصل الجزية
ما وضعت بصلح لا تغير، وحين غلبوا وأقروا على أملاكهم توضع على كتابي
اعلم أن الجزية نوعان:
فصل الجزية
١. جزية وضعت بالتراضي، فتقدّر بحسب ما يقع عليه الاتفاق. ٢. وجزية يبتدأ الإمام وضعها إذا غلب عليهم. (ما وضعت بصلح لا تغير، وحين غلبوا وأقروا على أملاكهم توضع)
على كتابي [١] قوله: فصل الجزية؛ لما فرغ من ذكر الوظائف المتعلقة بالأراضي شرع في ذكر الوظيفة التي توظف على رؤوس الكفّار، ويقال لها: خراج الرأس، والجزية – بالكسر -؛ لأنها تكفي وتجزئ عن القتل، وجمعه جزى كلحية ولحى، كذا في «البحر».
[٢] قوله: الاتفاق؛ أي بين المسلمين وبين الكفار كما صالح رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نصارى نجران على ألفي حلّة النصف في صفر، والبقية في رجب يؤدونها إلى المسلمين، وعارية ثلاثين درعاً.
(٣) قوله: وأقروا: أي أقرهم الإمام على أراضيهم وأملاكهم.
[٤] قوله: توضع؛ الأصل في هذا الباب قوله: ﴿قَاتِلُوا الَّذِينَ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ بِاللَّهِ وَلَا بِالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ وَلَا يُحَرِّمُونَ مَا حَرَّمَ اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ وَلَا يَدِينُونَ دِينَ الْحَقِّ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ عَنْ يَدٍ وَهُمْ صَاغِرُونَ﴾، قال مجاهد: نزلت هذه حين أمر محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه لله بغزوة تبوك، أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن جرير وغيرهما.
عمدة الرعاية: شرح الوقاية
ومجوسي
وقال ابن شهاب له: نزلت في كفار قريش والعرب: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ حَتَّى لَا تَكُونَ فِتْنَةٌ وَيَكُونَ الدِّينُ لِلَّهِ﴾، وأنزلت في أهل الكتاب هذه الآية، فكان أول من أعطى الجزية أهل نجران، أخرجه ابن المنذر.
وقال ابن عباس: سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن الجزية عن يد، قال: «جزية الأرض والرقبة»، أخرجه ابن أبي حاتم، فهذه الآية نص في أخذ الجزية من اليهود والنصارى. قال في «الفتح»: «ويدخل فيهم السّامرة، فإنّهم يدينون بشريعة موسى إلا أنهم يخالفونهم ويدخل فيهم الفرنج، وأمّا الصابئون فعلى الخلاف؛ فمن قال: هم من النصارى أو اليهود فهم من أهل الكتاب ومن قال: يعبدون الكواكب فهم من عبدة الأوثان». انتهى.
[١] قوله: ومجوسي؛ هو الذي يعبد النّار، وقد ثبت في «صحيح البخاري»: «إن عمر لم يكن أخذ الجزية من مجوس حتى شهد عبد الرحمن بن عوف أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذها من مجوس هجر»، وهذا نص على أن المجوس ليسوا بأهل كتاب، وإلا لم يتوقف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن حكم أخذ الجزية من أهل الكتاب في القرآن. وفي الباب أحاديث أخر في أخذ الجزية من المجوس، في «الموطأ»، و«مصنف ابن أبي شيبة»، و«معجم الطبراني» وغيرها على ما بسطه الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية)، وقد ضلّ من أباح النكاح بنساء المجوس ظنّاً منه أنهم من أهل الكتاب، وقد ذكرنا ما يتعلّق به في «كتاب النكاح».
Chapter of Jizya. What is set by treaty is not changed. And when they are overcome and allowed to keep their properties, it is imposed upon the Kitabi. Know that jizya is of two types: 1. Jizya set by mutual consent, so it is determined according to the agreement. 2. Jizya that the Imam initiates to impose when he overcomes them. (What is set by treaty is not changed, and when they are overcome and allowed to keep their properties, it is imposed upon the Kitabi.) [1] His saying: Chapter of Jizya; when he finished mentioning the functions related to lands, he began mentioning the function that is imposed upon the heads of the disbelievers, and it is called Kharaj al-Ra's (head tax). Jizya (with kasr) because it suffices and substitutes for killing. Its plural is jiza like lihya and liha, as in al-Bahr. [2] His saying: agreement; i.e., between Muslims and disbelievers as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ made peace with the Christians of Najran for two thousand garments, half in Safar and the remainder in Rajab, they pay them to the Muslims, and a loan of thirty coats of mail. (3) His saying: and they are allowed; i.e., the Imam allowed them to keep their lands and properties. [4] His saying: is imposed; the basis of this chapter is His saying: ﴿Fight those who do not believe in Allah nor the Last Day, nor forbid what Allah and His Messenger have forbidden, nor follow the religion of truth from among those who were given the Scripture until they give the jizya willingly while they are subdued.﴾ Mujahid said: This was revealed when Muhammad ﷺ and his Companions were commanded to the expedition of Tabuk, related by Ibn Abi Shaybah and Ibn Jarir and others. 'Umdat al-Ri'aya: Sharh al-Wiqaya. And Majusi. And Ibn Shihab said to him: It was revealed concerning the disbelievers of Quraysh and the Arabs: ﴿And fight them until there is no fitnah and the religion is for Allah.﴾ And this verse was revealed concerning the People of the Book. The first to give jizya were the people of Najran, related by Ibn al-Mundhir. And Ibn 'Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ was asked about 'an yad' (willingly) regarding jizya, he said: 'Jizya of land and neck.' Related by Ibn Abi Hatim. So this verse is clear text regarding taking jizya from Jews and Christians. He said in al-Fath: 'And the Samaritans are included, for they follow the law of Moses except that they differ; and the Franks are included. As for the Sabians, there is a difference of opinion: whoever says they are from the Christians or Jews, they are from the People of the Book; and whoever says they worship the planets, they are from the idol worshippers.' End. [1] His saying: and Majusi; it is one who worships fire. It is established in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Umar did not take jizya from the Magians until 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf testified that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ took it from the Magians of Hajar. This is clear text that the Magians are not people of a Book, otherwise the Messenger of Allah ﷺ would not have delayed concerning the ruling of taking jizya from the People of the Book in the Qur'an. And in this chapter are other hadiths on taking jizya from the Magians, in al-Muwatta', Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, and Mu'jam al-Tabarani and others, as detailed by al-Zayla'i in Takhrīj Ahādīth al-Hidāyah. And gone astray is the one who permitted marriage with Magian women, thinking they are from the People of the Book. We have mentioned what pertains to this in the Book of Marriage.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn on jizya. The author first defines jizya as a head tax imposed on non-Muslims under Muslim rule, explaining its linguistic meaning (it suffices/substitutes for killing). He then clarifies the two types: (1) jizya settled by mutual agreement between Muslims and the conquered people—this amount is fixed by treaty and cannot be changed; (2) jizya which the imam initiates and sets when he overcomes the people by force—this is based on his ijtihad. The base matn states that this jizya is imposed on Kitabis (People of the Book). The commentary provides the primary proof: the Quranic verse (al-Tawbah 9:29) commanding to fight People of the Book until they pay jizya. It quotes Mujahid that this was revealed regarding the expedition of Tabuk, and Ibn Shihab that another verse (al-Baqarah 2:193) was revealed for Arab polytheists, while the jizya verse is specifically for the People of the Book. The first to give jizya were the Christians of Najran, by treaty with the Prophet ﷺ. A hadith from Ibn 'Abbas explains 'an yad' as 'jizya of land and neck', meaning it is a tax on both land (kharaj) and the person. The passage then discusses who qualifies as 'Kitabi': it explicitly includes Samaritans and Franks (Europeans at that time) because they follow the Bible, but there is a dispute about Sabians—if they are considered Christian/Jewish they are Kitabi, otherwise idolaters. Finally, the passage addresses the Majus (Magians/Zoroastrians). It confirms that jizya is taken from them, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ who took it from the Magians of Hajar as witnessed by 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, and 'Umar's initial hesitation shows they are not Kitabi. The author warns against those who mistakenly consider Majus as People of the Book, leading to the error of permitting marriage with them. This passage thus establishes the ruling that jizya is taken from both Kitabis and Majus, with different evidential bases (Quran for the former, Sunnah for the latter).

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A head tax imposed on free, adult, non-Muslim men under Muslim rule in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
كتابي (kitābī): A person who follows a revealed scripture (Jew, Christian, etc.) and is thus eligible for jizya and dhimmi status.
مجوسي (majūsī): A fire-worshipper (Zoroastrian). The Hanafi school takes jizya from them based on prophetic practice, though they are not People of the Book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for taking jizya from the Majus (Magians)?
A) The Quranic verse explicitly includes them.
B) The practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions, as reported in authentic hadith.
C) They are considered People of the Book.
D) They voluntarily offered to pay.

Key Takeaway
Jizya is a head tax on Kitabis (Quran) and Majus (Sunnah); treaty-based jizya is fixed, while imam-imposed jizya is discretionary.

Basis for Taking Jizya from Jews, Christians, and Magians
Proofs from Quran and Sunnah for jizya on Jews, Christians, and Magians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya for Magians and explain the evidence from Quran and Sunnah that establishes it.

Core Idea
Jizya is wajib on Magians by Sunnah, not Quran, proving they are not People of the Book.

The obligation of jizya (poll tax) on non-Muslims is established by clear texts. This lesson examines the specific evidence for Jews, Christians, and Magians, highlighting how the Sunnah provides the basis for Magians, distinguishing them from Ahl al-Kitab. Understanding this distinction has practical implications for who is eligible for jizya and for related rulings such as marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage addresses the obligation of jizya on Jews, Christians, and Magians. Determine the hukm level (wajib) and who it applies to.
Jizya is a poll tax paid by eligible non-Muslims in exchange for protection.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence) for each group
For Jews and Christians, the Quranic verse (2:193) is cited. For Magians, the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet took jizya from the Magians of Hajar is used.
The Quranic verse commands fighting until fitnah ceases, but the specific application to Ahl al-Kitab is derived from other verses.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The imperative 'qātilū' in the Quran indicates obligation, but its connection to jizya is indirect; the hadith for Magians directly shows the Prophet's practice, making it a clear proof.
The hadith also implies Magians are not Ahl al-Kitab, because otherwise the Prophet would have relied on the Quran.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement) and Hanafi response
Some mistakenly consider Magians as Ahl al-Kitab, allowing marriage to their women. The Hanafi school refutes this based on the hadith's implication.
The author explicitly warns against this error.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The Hanafi position is that jizya is taken from Jews, Christians, and Magians, with Magians included by Sunnah evidence.
This is the ruling relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابن شهاب: له نزلت في كفار قريش والعرب: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ حَتَّى لَا تَكُونَ فِتْنَةٌ وَيَكُونَ الدِّينُ لِلَّهِ﴾، وأنزلت في أهل الكتاب هذه الآية، فكان أول من أعطى الجزية أهل نجران، أخرجه ابن المنذر. وقال ابن عباس: سئل رسولُ الله عن الجزية عن يد، قال: «جزية الأرض والرقبة»، أخرجه ابن أبي حاتم، فهذه الآية نص في أخذ الجزية من اليهود والنصارى. قال في «الفتح»: «ويدخل فيهم السّامرة، فإنّهم يدينون بشريعة موسى إلا أنهم يخالفونهم ويدخل فيهم الفرنج، وأمّا الصابئون فعلى الخلاف؛ فمن قال: هم من النصارى أو اليهود فهم من أهل الكتاب ومَن قال: يعبدون الكواكب فهم من عبدة الأوثان». انتهى. قوله: ومجوسي؛ هو الذي يعبدُ النّار، وقد ثبت في «صحيح البخاري»: «إنّ ه لم يكن أخذ الجزية من مجوس حتى شهد عبد الرحمن بن عوف: إنّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذها من مجوس هجر»، وهذا نص على أن المجوس ليسوا بأهل كتاب، وإلا لم يتوقف رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على ثبوت ذلك. حكم أخذ الجزية من أهل الكتاب في القرآن. وفي الباب أحاديث أخر في أخذ الجزية من المجوس، في «الموطأ»، و«مصنف ابن أبي شيبة»، و«معجم الطبراني» وغيرها على ما بسطه الزَّيْلَعِيُّ في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»، وقد ضلّ من أباح النكاح بنساء المجوس ظنّاً منه أنهم من أهل الكتاب، وقد ذكرنا ما يتعلّق به في «كتاب النكاح».
And Ibn Shihab said: It was revealed concerning the disbelievers of Quraysh and the Arabs: 'And fight them until there is no fitnah and the religion is for Allah,' and this verse was revealed concerning the People of the Book. So the first to give jizya were the people of Najran, narrated by Ibn al-Mundhir. And Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah was asked about jizya from the hand, he said: 'Jizya of the land and the neck,' narrated by Ibn Abi Hatim. So this verse is explicit about taking jizya from Jews and Christians. He said in al-Fath: 'And the Samaritans are included in them, for they follow the law of Moses except that they differ from them, and the Franks are included in them. As for the Sabians, there is disagreement: whoever says they are from the Christians or Jews, they are from the People of the Book, and whoever says they worship the stars, they are idol worshippers.' End. His saying: And Magian; he is the one who worships fire, and it is established in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Indeed, jizya was not taken from the Magians until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf testified that the Messenger of Allah took it from the Magians of Hajar,' and this is explicit that the Magians are not People of the Book, otherwise the Messenger of Allah would not have waited for that to be established. The ruling of taking jizya from the People of the Book is in the Quran. And in this chapter there are other hadiths about taking jizya from the Magians, in al-Muwatta, Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Mu'jam al-Tabarani and others as expanded by al-Zayla'i in Takhrīj Aḥādīth al-Hidāya. And he has gone astray who permits marriage to Magian women, thinking they are from the People of the Book, and we have mentioned what pertains to that in the Book of Marriage.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the basis for imposing jizya (poll tax) on non-Muslims. The author establishes that jizya is taken from Jews and Christians by explicit Quranic text (Surah al-Baqarah: 193) and from Magians (Zoroastrians) by the Sunnah, specifically the hadith where the Prophet took jizya from the Magians of Hajar after the testimony of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. This indicates that Magians are not Ahl al-Kitab (People of the Book), because if they were, the Prophet would have relied on the Quranic verse without need for this testimony. The author also clarifies that Samaritans and Franks are included with Jews and Christians, while Sabians are classified differently depending on their beliefs. A practical consequence: marrying Magian women is not permissible because they are not Ahl al-Kitab, contrary to those who mistakenly consider them so.

Key Terms
جزية (jizya): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslims in an Islamic state in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
مجوس (majūs): Zoroastrians, fire worshippers, distinct from Ahl al-Kitab in Hanafi view.
أهل الكتاب (ahl al-kitāb): People of the Book: Jews, Christians, and according to some, Samaritans and Franks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Jews
B) Christians
C) Magians
D) Idol worshippers

Key Takeaway
Jizya is taken from Jews and Christians by Quran and from Magians by Sunnah, confirming Magians are not People of the Book.

Jizya on Polytheist Non-Arabs: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi ruling on jizya for polytheist non-Arabs and rebuttal of Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jizya for polytheist non-Arabs, explain the proofs, and respond to the Shafi'i objection using qiyas.

Core Idea
Jizya is taken from polytheist non-Arabs because the general command to fight all disbelievers is only lifted for specific groups.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding who is eligible to pay jizya. Imam Shafi'i restricts jizya to Ahl al-Kitab and Magians, while the Hanafis include polytheist non-Arabs. The reasoning hinges on the general obligation of jihad and an analogy to the permissibility of enslavement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine the exact point of dispute: whether jizya is imposed on polytheist non-Arabs (وثني عجمي).
Not in dispute: Ahl al-Kitab and Magians pay jizya; Arab polytheists do not.
2
State the Hanafi position and primary proof
The Hanafi school holds that jizya is wajib on polytheist non-Arabs. The primary proof is the general command to fight all disbelievers (Quran 2:193), from which only specific groups are exempted by other texts.
The imperative indicates obligation; exceptions are limited to Ahl al-Kitab (by verse) and Magians (by hadith).
3
Explain the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that jizya is only for Ahl al-Kitab and Magians, not for idol worshippers, based on the same texts but reading them as exhaustive exceptions.
Shafi'i considers the exceptions as limiting the general command definitively.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response using qiyas
The Hanafi response uses qiyas: since it is agreed that polytheist non-Arabs can be enslaved (istiqrāq), they can also be subjected to jizya, by analogy to Magians. An objection about women and children is answered: they can be enslaved but are not suitable subjects (mahall) for jizya.
The analogy is based on the common attribute: both groups are disbelievers not specifically exempted, and their enslavement is permissible.
5
Note the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: if a polytheist non-Arab refuses to pay jizya, Hanafis would fight them, while Shafi'is would consider them not subject to jizya and thus must be fought or converted without that option.
The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووثني عجمي ظهر غناه، فيه خلافُ الشَّافِعِي، فإنَّه لا توضع عليه، لكلِّ سنة ثمانية وأربعون درهما: يأخذ في كل شهر أربعة دراهم، (وعلى المتوسط نصفها، وعلى فقير يكسب ربعها) قوله: ووثني؛ - بفتحتين - نسبة إلى الوثن: أي عابد الصنم من غير العرب، وأما المشرك العربي فلا جزية عليه على ما سيأتي. قوله: ظهر غناه؛ الجملة صفة لكل من الثلاثة. قال في «الكفاية»: الظاهر الغنى: هو صاحب المال الكثير الذي لا يحتاج إلى العمل. والمتوسط: الذي له مال لا يستغني به عن العمل. والمعتمل: من يكسب أكثر من حاجته ولا مال له. قوله: عنده؛ لأن قتال الكفار واجب بنص: ﴿وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ حَتَّى لَا تَكُونَ فِتْنَةٌ وَيَكُونَ الدين لله﴾، إلا أنه عرف جواز تركه في حق أهل الكتاب بالآية، وفي حق المجوس بالخبر، فيبقى ما وراءهما على الأصل. ونحن نقول: إنّ عبدة الأوثان يجوز استرقاقهم اتفاقاً، فيجوز أخذ الجزية منهم كما يجوز أخذها من المجوس، وهم عبدة النار. فإن قلت: النساء والصبيان يجوز استرقاقهم مع أنه لا يجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم. قلت: هناك المحل غير قابل، فكل من يجوز استرقاقهم يجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم إذا كان المحلّ قابلاً، كذا في «العناية» قوله: وعلى المتوسط نصفها؛ أي أربعة وعشرون درهماً هذا التفصيل مأثور عن عمر، أخرجه ابن أبي شَيْبَة، وابن زنجويه في «كتاب الأموال».
And a polytheist non-Arab whose wealth is apparent; there is disagreement with al-Shafi'i, for he does not impose it on him; each year forty-eight dirhams: he takes four dirhams every month. (And for the middle-class half of that, and for a poor earner one-fourth of it). His saying: 'and a polytheist' - with two faths - relating to idol: meaning an idol worshipper from non-Arabs; as for an Arab polytheist, there is no jizya on him as will come. His saying: 'whose wealth is apparent' - the phrase is an attribute for each of the three. He said in al-Kifaya: the apparent wealthy: he is the owner of abundant wealth who does not need to work. The middle-class: he who has wealth but still needs to work. The laborer: he who earns more than his need but has no wealth. His saying: 'according to him' - because fighting the disbelievers is obligatory by the text: 'And fight them until there is no fitnah and the religion is for Allah,' except that it is known that leaving it is permissible for the People of the Book by the verse, and for the Magians by the report, so what is beyond them remains on the original. And we say: indeed, it is agreed that idol worshippers can be enslaved, so it is permissible to take jizya from them just as it is permissible to take it from the Magians, who are fire worshippers. If you say: women and children can be enslaved, yet jizya is not imposed on them. I say: there the subject is not suitable; so whoever can be enslaved, jizya can be imposed on them if the subject is suitable, as in al-Inaya. His saying: 'and for the middle-class half of that' - meaning twenty-four dirhams; this detail is transmitted from Umar, narrated by Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Zanjawayh in Kitab al-Amwal.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding jizya on polytheist non-Arabs (وثني عجمي). Imam Shafi'i holds that no jizya is imposed on them, while the Hanafi school argues that it is wajib. The Hanafi proof: the general command to fight all disbelievers is only excepted for Ahl al-Kitab (by Quran) and Magians (by Sunnah); polytheist non-Arabs fall under the original rule of fighting, but jizya can substitute for killing if they pay. Furthermore, since it is agreed that they can be enslaved, it follows that they can also be required to pay jizya, by analogy to the Magians. An objection concerning women and children (who can be enslaved but not jizya) is answered: their enslavement is possible but they are not suitable subjects for jizya (e.g., due to incapacity). The rates are set: wealthy pay 48 dirhams/year, middle-class 24, and poor earners 12, based on Umar's practice.

Key Terms
وثني عجمي (wathanī ʿajamī): A non-Arab idol worshipper; polytheist from lands other than Arabia.
مشرك عربي (mushrik ʿarabī): An Arab polytheist; no jizya is taken from them; they must either accept Islam or be fought.
استرقاق (istiqrāq): Enslavement of war captives; used here as evidence for permissibility of jizya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Women and children are not capable of paying jizya.
B) The subject for jizya requires the ability to pay, which women and children lack.
C) Enslavement is a separate ruling; jizya only applies to those who are suitable subjects (e.g., free adult males).
D) Women and children must pay jizya as well according to Hanafi.

Key Takeaway
Jizya is wajib on polytheist non-Arabs in the Hanafi school, based on the general command to fight and analogy to Magians and enslavement.

Jizya Not on Arab Polytheists: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on jizya exemption for Arab polytheists with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya from Arab polytheists and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Jizya is not taken from Arab polytheists; they face Islam or the sword.

The Hanafi school holds that jizya is not accepted from Arab polytheists; upon conquest, they are given the choice of Islam or the sword. The Shafi'i school argues that jizya is taken from every adult, including Arab polytheists, relying on the hadith of Mu'adh. This lesson examines the proofs and the Hanafi rebuttal, which centers on interpreting that hadith as applying only to treaty jizya (jizya al-sulh).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: jizya is not accepted from Arab polytheists. When conquered, they become prisoners of war (slaves or killed) unless they embrace Islam.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that jizya is taken from every adult, male and female, based on the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Take from every adult a dinar or its equivalent.'
Also recorded with the phrase 'every adult male and female'.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
Hanafi scholars respond that the hadith is interpreted as referring to jizya al-sulh (treaty jizya), not jizya al-'anwah (conquest jizya). The key evidence is that the hadith includes women, whereas war jizya is only taken from men.
4
Analyse the rebuttal's strength
The inclusion of women in the hadith indicates it was a treaty arrangement, as women are not subject to jizya in conquest. Thus, the Shafi'i proof does not apply to the case of Arab polytheists conquered in war.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi says Arab polytheists cannot be allowed to remain on jizya; they must convert or be fought. Shafi'i allows them to pay jizya and remain in their religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا على وثني عربي، فإن ظهر عليه، فعرسه وعند الشَّافِعِي" (1)[1] على كل حالم وحالمة دينار، الفقير والغني سواء.
(لا على وثني عربي"، فإن ظهر عليه ، فعرسه سعد في «الطبقات (۲) ، وأبو عبيد القاسم ابن سلام في «كتاب الأموال»(۳). [1]قوله : وعند الشافعي ... الخ ؛ حجته حديث معاذ بن جبل : «إنه أمره رسول الله حين بعثه على اليمن أن يأخذ من كل حالم ديناراً أو عدله معافر : وهي شياب تكون باليمن ) ، أخرجه أبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن حبان، والحاكم، وغيرهم. (٤) وورد في مصنف عبد الرزاق»، و «سنن الدارقطني»، و«مسند إسحاق ابن راهويه»، وغيرها: «على كل حالم وحالمة»). وأجاب عنه أصحابنا بأنه محمول على جزية الصلح ؛ ولهذا أمره بالأخذ من الحالمة وإن كانت لا تؤخذ منها الجزية. كذا في «الهداية».
Not on an Arab polytheist, and if one is conquered, he becomes a prisoner. According to al-Shafi'i: On every adult male and female, a dinar, the poor and the rich are equal. (Not on an Arab polytheist, and if conquered, he becomes a prisoner) Sa'd in al-Tabaqat and Abu 'Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam in Kitab al-Amwal. [1] His statement: 'And according to al-Shafi'i...' his proof is the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'The Messenger of Allah, when he sent him to Yemen, ordered him to take from every adult a dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir garments, which are garments from Yemen.' Narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, Ibn Hibban, al-Hakim, and others. And it is reported in the Musannaf of 'Abd al-Razzaq, Sunan al-Daraqutni, Musnad of Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, and others: 'On every adult male and female.' Our companions answered that it is interpreted as jizya of treaty; for this reason he ordered taking from the adult female even though jizya is not taken from her. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding on whom jizya is obligatory. The Hanafi ruling is that jizya is not taken from Arab polytheists; if they are conquered, they are enslaved or killed unless they embrace Islam. The Shafi'i school holds that jizya is taken from every adult, male or female, poor or rich, based on the hadith of Mu'adh. The Hanafi response, as stated in Al-Hidayah, is that the hadith refers to jizya al-sulh (treaty jizya), not jizya al-‘anwah (conquest jizya). Evidence includes that Mu'adh was ordered to take from women, whereas war jizya is only taken from men. Thus the Shafi'i proof does not apply to the case of conquest jizya.

Key Terms
وثني عربي (wathanī 'arabī): An Arab polytheist, i.e., an idol worshiper from the Arabian Peninsula.
جزية الصلح (jizyat al-ṣulḥ): Jizya imposed by treaty, where terms are agreed upon, as opposed to jizya imposed by conquest.
حالم (ḥālim): An adult who has reached puberty (literally 'dreamer', one who has wet dreams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It applies only to non-Arabs
D) It was said before the revelation of jizya verses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between treaty jizya (which can include women and Arabs) and conquest jizya (which is only from non-Arab men); the hadith of Mu'adh falls into the former category.

Jizya for Apostates and Arab Polytheists: Only Islam or Death
Ruling on apostates and Arab polytheists: only Islam or sword accepted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizya for apostates and Arab polytheists and explain the dispute with the Shafi'i school using the dalil from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Apostates and Arab polytheists: only Islam or the sword; no jizya, no enslavement.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that jizya cannot be accepted from apostates (murtadd) or Arab polytheists (wathanī 'arabī). The only options are conversion to Islam or execution. This rule is contrasted with the Shafi'i view that Arab polytheists may be enslaved. The proof is based on a narration from Mujahid indicating the Prophet fought idolaters exclusively for Islam.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that jizya is not accepted from apostates or Arab polytheists; they must convert or be killed.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i allows enslaving Arab polytheists, analogizing them to other polytheists.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The text cites a narration from Mujahid that the Prophet fought idolaters over Islam, not for jizya. The reasoning: Arab disbelief is more severe because the Prophet was Arab and the Qur'an in Arabic, so only Islam is accepted.
The dalil is naqli, based on practice of the Prophet.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi, Arab polytheists cannot become dhimmis; under Shafi'i, they may.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon one in the madhhab.
Authority: Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text

This passage presents the Hanafi ruling that apostates and Arab polytheists are not eligible for jizya; only Islam or death is accepted. The proof is the narration from Mujahid that the Prophet fought idolaters over Islam, indicating the severity of their shirk. The commentary then explains the terms: 'booty' refers to spoils divided after khums; 'apostate' is one who leaves Islam and is executed if not returning; 'Arab polytheists' can be enslaved according to Shafi'i but the Hanafi response is that they must either convert or be executed, not enslaved, because jizya is not accepted. The monk mention here introduces the next ruling.

Jizya on Secluded Monks: Ability to Work as Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jizya for secluded monks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on jizya for secluded monks and apply the condition of ability to work to determine when jizya is imposed.

Core Idea
A monk who can work but secludes himself must pay jizya, like one who neglects kharaj land.

This lesson examines a debated case within the Hanafi school: whether monks who seclude themselves from society are subject to jizya. The matn suggests they are exempt, but the commentary reveals that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf held that jizya is imposed if the monk is able to work. We will trace the reasoning and identify the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
Muhammad reports that Abu Hanifa used to say jizya is imposed on monks if they are able to work. Another narration from Abu Hanifa exempts them entirely because they are not fighters.
The first narration is also the view of Abu Yusuf.
2
Understand the reasoning behind exemption
The exemption view argues that jizya is a substitute for killing (isqat al-qatl). A secluded monk is not killed in war, so no jizya.
This is based on the original purpose of jizya.
3
Understand the reasoning for imposition
The imposition view uses istihsan via analogy to kharaj land: the monk wasted his ability to work, just as a cultivator who neglects land still owes kharaj.
This is the reasoning given in al-Hidayah.
4
Identify the relied-upon position
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah prefers the view that jizya is imposed when the monk is able to work. This is the mufta bihi.
Ability to work is defined as not being chronically ill or having an impediment to earning.
5
Apply the condition of ability
If the monk is able to work (physically capable), jizya is required. If he is disabled or elderly, jizya is not imposed.
The condition is explicitly mentioned in the passage: 'قادراً'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤] قوله : لا يخالط ؛ فأما الرهبان والقسيسون الذين يخالطون الناس فقال محمد : كان أبو حنيفة الا الله يقول بوضع الجزية عليهم إذا كانوا يقدرون على العمل، وهو قول أبي يوسف . كذا في «شرح مختصر القُدُورِيّ» للأَقْطَع. والوجه فيه : إن من لا يقتل لا توضع عليه الجزية ؛ فإنّ الجزية لإسقاط القتل، وغير المخالط لا يقتل فلا جزية عليه. [0]قوله : توضـع ؛ قال في «الهداية»(۳) : وجه الوضع عليهم : أن القدرة على العمل، هوا الذي ضيعها فصار كتعطيل الأرض الخراجية، ووجه الوضع عنهم قد مرّ. [٦] قوله : قادراً ؛ بأن لم يكن زَمِناً ولا به علة مانعة من الكسب.
[4] His statement: 'who does not mix' - as for the monks and priests who mix with people, Muhammad said: Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) used to say that jizya is imposed on them if they are able to work, and that is the statement of Abu Yusuf. Thus in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta'. And the face of it: He who is not killed does not have jizya imposed on him; because jizya is for the removal of killing, and the one who does not mix is not killed, so no jizya on him. [5] His statement: 'imposed' - he said in al-Hidayah: The face of imposing on them is that the ability to work, he is the one who wasted it, so it becomes like the neglect of kharaji land, and the face of not imposing has passed. [6] His statement: 'able' - meaning he is not chronically ill nor has an impediment preventing earning.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage addresses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether monks who do not mix with society (i.e., those who seclude themselves) are subject to jizya. The matn states jizya is not taken from such monks. The commentary explains two positions: Abu Hanifa (according to a narration from Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf hold that jizya is imposed on them if they are able to work, because their seclusion is voluntary, like wasting agricultural land. The opposing view (also attributed to Abu Hanifa in another narration) is that they are exempt because they are not fighters and jizya is a substitute for killing, and since such monks are not killed, no jizya. The relied-upon view appears to be the condition of ability: if they can work but choose not to, jizya is imposed; if they are unable (old, sick), no jizya. This reasoning uses rational analogy (qiyas) with kharaj land neglect.

Key Terms
راهب (rāhib): A monk, specifically one who does not mix with society (لا يخالط)
قادراً على العمل (qādiran 'alā al-'amal): Able to work, i.e., physically capable of earning a living through labor or craft.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he is a priest
B) When he is able to work
C) When he is elderly
D) Never, because monks are exempt

Key Takeaway
Jizya on secluded monks depends on ability to work; those able but avoiding work must pay, analogous to wasting productive land.

Jizyah Not Accepted from Apostates or Arab Polytheists
Ruling and proof that apostates and Arab polytheists are not offered jizyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jizyah for apostates and Arab polytheists, and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Apostates and Arab polytheists are not offered jizyah—only Islam or the sword.

This lesson examines a distinctive Hanafi ruling: jizyah is not accepted from apostates or Arab polytheists. The passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that while other non-Muslims may pay jizyah, these two categories are excluded. We will explore the proof from hadith and the rationale that Arab polytheism is more severe due to the Prophet's lineage and the Qur'an's language. A comparison with the Shafi'i position will highlight the practical differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excluded categories
The passage explicitly names two groups: apostates (murtadd) and Arab polytheists (wathani 'arabi). They are not offered jizyah.
Apostates are former Muslims; Arab polytheists are idolaters from the Arab lineage.
2
Understand the child as booty
The opening phrase 'وطفله فيء' states that the child of a slain polytheist is war booty (fay'), not a candidate for jizyah.
This reinforces that the polytheists themselves are to be fought, not taxed.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The hadith from Mujahid: 'The idolaters are fought over Islam, and the People of the Book are fought over jizyah.' This provides the primary textual evidence.
The hadith distinguishes between two groups, implying jizyah is only for People of the Book.
4
Analyze the rationale
The commentary explains that Arab polytheism is more severe because the Prophet ﷺ was Arab and the Qur'an was revealed in Arabic. Thus, only full submission (Islam) is acceptable.
This rationale supports excluding Arab polytheists from the jizyah option.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i allows jizyah from Arab polytheists and even their enslavement. Hanafis reject this based on the hadith and the special severity of Arab disbelief.
The practical difference: Hanafis fight Arab polytheists until Islam or death; Shafi'is may take jizyah or enslave them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الجهاد / فصل الجزية
وطفله فيء، ولا مرتد، ولا يقبل منهما إلا الإسلام أو السيف. قوله: وطفله فيء أي غنيمة تقسم بين الغانمين بعد رفع الخمس، وأما رجال المشركين فيقتلون إلا أن يسلموا. قوله: ولا مرتد أي لا تقبل من المرتد وهو الذي ارتد عن دين الإسلام الجزية، بل يقتل إن لم يسلم على ما سيأتي. قوله: ولا يقبل منهما إلا الإسلام أو السيف أي من الوثني العربي والمرتد. وعند الشافعي يسترق مشركو العرب. قوله: مشركو العرب أي يجوز أن يجعل مشركو العرب وهم بالغون أرقاء من دون قتل وقد مر جوابه. وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة والبيهقي عن مجاهد قال: يقاتل أهل الأوثان على الإسلام، ويقاتل أهل الكتاب على الجزية. والوجه فيه: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما كان منهم أي العرب والقرآن بلغتهم، فكان كفر العرب أغلظ من كفر غيرهم، فلا يقبل منهم إلا الإسلام.
Book of Jihad / Chapter of Jizyah. And his child is booty, and not an apostate, and nothing is accepted from the two except Islam or the sword. His statement: 'and his child is booty' meaning spoils divided among the fighters after removing the khums. As for the polytheist men, they are killed unless they accept Islam. His statement: 'and not an apostate' meaning jizyah is not accepted from the apostate, who is one who apostatized from the religion of Islam; rather he is killed if he does not accept Islam, as will come. His statement: 'and nothing is accepted from the two except Islam or the sword' meaning from the Arab polytheist and the apostate. According to al-Shafi'i, Arab polytheists can be enslaved. His statement: 'Arab polytheists' meaning it is permissible to make adult Arab polytheists slaves without killing, and its answer has passed. And Ibn Abi Shayba and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Mujahid: 'The idolaters are fought over Islam, and the People of the Book are fought over jizyah.' The reasoning is that the Prophet ﷺ was from them, i.e. the Arabs, and the Qur'an was in their language, so the disbelief of the Arabs is more severe than the disbelief of others, so nothing is accepted from them except Islam.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah (via commentary), addressing the categories of non-Muslims from whom jizyah is not accepted. The Hanafi position is clear: jizyah is not taken from an apostate (murtadd) or an Arab polytheist (wathani 'arabi). For apostates, the option is only Islam or death; for Arab polytheists, the same applies, unlike other polytheists (e.g., non-Arabs) for whom jizyah is permissible according to some. The commentary explains that the child of a slain polytheist becomes booty (fay'), divided after khums. The Shafi'i school differs, allowing enslavement of Arab polytheists without killing. The Hanafi proof is a hadith from Mujahid stating that idolaters are fought over Islam, while People of the Book are fought over jizyah. The rationale is that Arab disbelief is more severe due to the Prophet being Arab and the Qur'an in Arabic. The author follows the order of the matn, explaining each phrase before moving to the next.

Key Terms
فيء (fay'): Spoils of war taken from the enemy without fighting (in this context, booty including the child of a slain polytheist).
مرتد (murtadd): One who apostatizes from Islam; jizyah is not accepted from him, only Islam or death.
الجزية (al-jizyah): The poll tax levied on non-Muslims (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Jizyah is not accepted from apostates or Arab polytheists; they must be fought until Islam or death.

Jizyah on Secluded Monks: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jizyah for secluded monks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on jizyah for secluded monks, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement, and apply the qiyas used.

Core Idea
Jizyah on a monk depends on his ability to work; seclusion alone does not guarantee exemption.

This passage addresses a nuanced case: monks who withdraw from society entirely. The Hanafi school recognizes a difference between those who can work and those who cannot. The root text exempts the non-mixing monk from jizyah, but a counter-narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad imposes it if the monk is capable. Understanding this requires parsing the rationale of jizyah as ransom for life.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling in the matn
The matn says jizyah is not on a rahib who does not mix with people. This is the starting point.
The term 'rahb' here implies a monk who lives in seclusion, not one who participates in society.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi objection
Abu Yusuf and a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa hold that jizyah is imposed on such a monk if he is capable of work.
This shows the school is not monolithic; there is a valid ikhtilaf even among the founders.
3
Understand the rationale for exemption
The text gives a reason: jizyah is for sparing killing (blood money); the non-mixing monk is not a target of killing, so no jizyah.
This is a dalil based on the purpose (hikmah) of jizyah.
4
Examine the qiyas for imposition
The opposing view uses analogy to kharaj land: just as kharaj is due on uncultivated land because the owner wasted its potential, jizyah is due on a capable monk who wastes his ability to earn.
The illa is the wasting of the ability to work by choice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a monk capable of work but secluded may or may not pay jizyah depending on which view is followed. The mufta bihi is to impose if capable, exempt if incapable.
This affects real-life fatwa application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا على راهب لا يخالط. وعند أبي يوسف له، وهو رواية محمد عن أبي حنيفة توضع إن كان قادراً على العمل. قوله: لا يخالط؛ فأما الرهبان والقسيسون الذين يخالطون الناس فقال محمد: كان أبو حنيفة يقول بوضع الجزية عليهم إذا كانوا يقدرون على العمل، وهو قول أبي يوسف. كذا في شرح مختصر القدوري للأقطع. والوجه فيه: إن من لا يقتل لا توضع عليه الجزية؛ فإن الجزية لإسقاط القتل، وغير المخالط لا يقتل فلا جزية عليه. قوله: توضع؛ قال في الهداية: وجه الوضع عليهم: أن القدرة على العمل هو الذي ضيعها فصار كتعطيل الأرض الخراجية، ووجه الوضع عنهم قد مر.
And not on a monk who does not mix [with people]. According to Abu Yusuf, it is [imposed?] on him, and it is a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa that it is imposed if he is capable of work. His statement: 'who does not mix'; as for the monks and priests who mix with people, Muhammad said: Abu Hanifa used to say that jizyah is imposed on them if they are able to work, and this is also the statement of Abu Yusuf. Thus in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta'. The reasoning: The one who is not killed has jizyah not imposed on him; for jizyah is for the removal of killing, and the non-mixing monk is not killed, so no jizyah on him. His statement: 'imposed'; said in al-Hidayah: The reason for imposing on them is that the ability to work is what he has wasted, so it is like the abandonment of kharaj land. And the reason for not imposing on them has already passed.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about jizyah on monks (ruhban) who live in seclusion and do not mix with people. The base text states that jizyah is not imposed on such a monk. The commentary then clarifies that according to Abu Yusuf, jizyah is imposed on any monk who is capable of work, and this is also a narration from Muhammad from Abu Hanifa. However, the preferred position (mufta bihi) seems to be the opposite: monks who neither mix nor are capable of work are exempt. The rationale is that jizyah is a replacement for killing, and since such a monk is not killed (due to his harmless status), no jizyah is due. On the other hand, if a monk is able to work but chooses not to, jizyah is imposed by analogy with kharaj land that is left uncultivated. The author quotes al-Hidayah to show both sides.

Key Terms
راهب (rahb): Monk; specifically one who secludes himself for worship and does not mix with society.
مخالط (mukhalit): One who mixes with people; in this context, a monk who interacts with society and can work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, on which type of monk is jizyah imposed?
A) A monk who does not mix with people and is incapable of work
B) A monk who mixes with people and is capable of work
C) All monks without exception
D) No monk ever pays jizyah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts a monk who is unable to work and does not mix; but if he is capable, there is a valid intra-school difference.
